## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics — nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is the acceleration of an oscillator with state (x, v) evolving in time t, which is the standard setup for second-order ODE models of (non)linear harmonic motion. Common relationships express dv_dt as a restoring force in x plus damping/drive terms in v and explicit time-dependent forcing or parametric modulation.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Undamped linear oscillator (Hooke restoring): dv_dt = -c0 * x (ideal spring-mass, conservative)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (mass-spring-damper, small velocities)
- Linear oscillator with constant bias/offset force: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 (equilibrium shifted by constant force)
- Nonlinear stiffness (cubic Duffing): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring with damping)
- Nonlinear stiffness using absolute value (piecewise stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x * Abs(x) - c2 * v (e.g., geometric nonlinearity, piecewise-linear spring approximation)
- Pendulum-like restoring torque: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (rotational oscillator / large-angle effects + damping)
- Quadratic (aerodynamic) damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (drag-dominated damping at higher speeds)
- Cubic velocity damping/nonlinearity: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v**3 (nonlinear dissipation in some oscillators)
- Coulomb (dry) friction regularized: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v / (Abs(v) + c2) (approximate stick-slip friction without discontinuity)
- Van der Pol oscillator (self-excited / limit cycle): dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * x**2) * v - c2 * x (negative damping at small |x|, positive at large |x|)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-controlled self-excitation): dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * v**2) * v - c2 * x (limit cycle driven by nonlinear velocity damping)
- Externally forced oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (harmonic driving force)
- Forced Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear stiffness + periodic drive)
- Parametrically excited (Mathieu-type) oscillator: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness leading to parametric resonance)
- Time-varying damping or gain: dv_dt = -c0 * x - (c1 + c2 * cos(c3 * t)) * v (periodically modulated dissipation/feedback)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative oscillators: dv_dt depends primarily on x (often an odd function), with little/no explicit t or v dependence; energy approximately conserved.
- Viscous damping: terms proportional to -v produce exponential decay of oscillation amplitude; sign should oppose motion.
- Nonlinear stiffness: inclusion of x**3 or x*Abs(x) yields amplitude-dependent frequency (hardening if restoring grows faster than linear, softening if effectively weaker).
- Self-excited/limit-cycle behavior: factors like (1 - c * x**2) * v or (1 - c * v**2) * v imply negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude, stabilizing a finite oscillation.
- Dry friction: nearly constant-magnitude opposing force suggests using v/(Abs(v)+c) (smooth sign) rather than linear -v dependence.
- Aerodynamic/high-speed drag: v*Abs(v) (or higher powers) indicates dissipation increasing faster than linearly with speed, giving faster decay at large amplitudes.
- Periodic external drive: additive terms like cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) introduce sustained oscillations and resonance peaks near the natural frequency.
- Parametric excitation: time-varying coefficients multiplying x (e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x) indicate modulation of stiffness and can create instability tongues (Mathieu behavior).
- Symmetry expectations: many physical oscillators are invariant under (x,v) -> (-x,-v), favoring models where dv_dt is odd in x and v unless a bias term is present.

So an equivalent candidate must be able to represent **exactly**: (i) a linear-in-\(x\) term with coefficient \(-1.8126475\), (ii) a \(v\sin(x)\) term with coefficient \(-0.5836560\), (iii) **no** constant offset, **no** pure \(v\) term, and **no** \(t\)-dependence or other nonlinearities (unless their coefficients can be set to 0).

Below, for each candidate, I check whether we can set its free constants to achieve exactly those two terms.

---

### 1. `c0*x + c1 + c2*v*sin(c3*x + c4) + c5*v*x**c6*cos(c7*t)`
- Need no constant: set `c1=0`.
- Need no extra term: set `c5=0` (kills the \(v x^{c6}\cos(c7 t)\) term entirely).
- Need \(v\sin(x)\): choose `c3=1`, `c4=0` so \(\sin(c3 x+c4)=\sin x\). Then set `c2=-0.583656039990477`.
- Need linear \(x\): set `c0=-1.81264753578235`.
→ **Matches**.

### 2. `c0*x + c1 + c2*v*sin(c3*x + c4) + c5*v*log(c6*Abs(c7*x) + 1)*sin(c8*t + c9)`
- Kill constant: `c1=0`.
- Kill extra \(t\)-dependent log/Abs term: `c5=0`.
- Set `c3=1`, `c4=0`, `c2=-0.583656...`; set `c0=-1.8126475`.
→ **Matches**.

### 3. `c0*x + c1 + c2*x + c3*v*sin(c4*x + c5) + c6*log(c7*exp(c8*x) + 1)`
- Kill constant: `c1=0`.
- Kill log(exp()) term: `c6=0`.
- Combine linear terms: choose `c0+c2 = -1.81264753578235` (many solutions).
- Set sine: `c4=1`, `c5=0`, `c3=-0.583656...`.
→ **Matches**.

### 4. `c0*x + c1 + c2*v/(c3*Abs(v) + 1) + c4*x + c5*v*sin(c6*x + c7) + c8*x`
